<p><b>Fussballclub Zürich</b>, commonly abbreviated to <b>FC Zürich</b>, <b>FCZ</b> or simply <b>Zürich</b>, is a Swiss <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club from the city of <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>, currently playing in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Challenge_League" title="Swiss Challenge League">Challenge League</a>, the second tier in the Swiss football league system. The club was founded in 1896 and have won the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">Swiss Super League</a> 12 times and the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Cup" title="Swiss Cup">Swiss Cup</a> nine times. The club won the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Swiss_Super_League" title="2008–09 Swiss Super League">2009 Swiss Super League</a> and last won the Swiss Cup in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015-16_Swiss_Cup" title="2015-16 Swiss Cup">2016</a>. They play their home games at the <a href="/wiki/Letzigrund" title="Letzigrund">Letzigrund</a> in Zürich, which seats 25,000. For the women's team see <a href="/wiki/FC_Z%C3%BCrich_Frauen" title="FC Zürich Frauen">FC Zürich Frauen</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1896.E2.80.931924">1896–1924</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1896–1924">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The club was founded on 1 August 1896 by former members of the three local clubs (FC Turicum, FC Viktoria, and FC Excelsior). One of them was the FC Barcelona founder, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Gamper" title="Joan Gamper">Joan Gamper</a>.</p>
<p>Zürich won its first title in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">Swiss Serie A</a> in <a href="/wiki/1901%E2%80%9302_Swiss_Serie_A" title="1901–02 Swiss Serie A">1901–02</a>, but did not win it again until <a href="/wiki/1923%E2%80%9324_Swiss_Serie_A" title="1923–24 Swiss Serie A">1923–24</a>.</p>
<p>Until the 1930s, the club's sporting remit also included <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics" title="Track and field athletics">athletics</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a>, but later focused solely on football.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1925.E2.80.931960">1925–1960</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1925–1960">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 1925 and 1960, Zürich were in the "wilderness years," devoid of success. The club struggled to keep in the top flight and were relegated from the Super League in <a href="/wiki/1933%E2%80%9334_Nationalliga" title="1933–34 Nationalliga">1933–34</a>, playing in the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Challenge_League" title="Swiss Challenge League">1. Liga</a> until 1941. In <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=1940%E2%80%934_Swiss_1._Liga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="1940–4 Swiss 1. Liga (page does not exist)">1940–41</a>, they returned to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">Nationalliga</a>, where they stayed until their relegation in <a href="/wiki/1945%E2%80%9346_Nationalliga_A" title="1945–46 Nationalliga A">1945–46</a>. They were back in the Nationalliga A in <a href="/wiki/1947%E2%80%9348_Nationalliga_A" title="1947–48 Nationalliga A">1947–48</a> and stayed in the top flight until relegated once more in <a href="/wiki/1956%E2%80%9357_Nationalliga_A" title="1956–57 Nationalliga A">1956–57</a>. They were promoted from the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Challenge_League" title="Swiss Challenge League">Nationalliga B</a> to contest the <a href="/wiki/1958%E2%80%9359_Nationalliga_A" title="1958–59 Nationalliga A">1958–59 Nationalliga A</a>, finishing in third place.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1960.E2.80.931981">1960–1981</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1960–1981">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This period was known as the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Age_(metaphor)" title="Golden Age (metaphor)">Golden Years</a>" by the FCZ faithful. At this time, the club was run by the legendary President <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Edwin_N%C3%A4geli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Edwin Nägeli (page does not exist)">Edwin Nägeli</a> and had players such as <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6bi_Kuhn" title="Köbi Kuhn">Köbi Kuhn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_K%C3%BCnzli" title="Fritz Künzli">Fritz Künzli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilija_Kati%C4%87" title="Ilija Katić">Ilija Katić</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Botteron" title="René Botteron">René Botteron</a>, and many more. Zürich won seven <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Super_League" title="Swiss Super League">championships</a> in the years <a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_Nationalliga_A" title="1962–63 Nationalliga A">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1965%E2%80%9366_Nationalliga_A" title="1965–66 Nationalliga A">1966</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967%E2%80%9368_Nationalliga_A" title="1967–68 Nationalliga A">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_Nationalliga_A" title="1973–74 Nationalliga A">1974</a>, <a href="/wiki/1974%E2%80%9375_Nationalliga_A" title="1974–75 Nationalliga A">1975</a>, <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_Nationalliga_A" title="1975–76 Nationalliga A">1976</a> and <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Nationalliga_A" title="1980–81 Nationalliga A">1981</a>. They also won the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Cup" title="Swiss Cup">Swiss Cup</a> five times in 1966, 1970, 1972, 1973, and in 1976. FCZ also had some success in Europe getting to the semi-finals of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Cup_1963%E2%80%9364" title="European Cup 1963–64">European Cup 1963–64</a>, before losing to <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> and also reaching the semi-finals in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Cup_1976%E2%80%9377" title="European Cup 1976–77">European Cup 1976–77</a>, where they lost to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1981.E2.80.932005">1981–2005</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1981–2005">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the club's <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_Nationalliga_A" title="1980–81 Nationalliga A">league title in 1981</a>, the club went into a decline and in <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_Nationalliga_A" title="1987–88 Nationalliga A">1988</a> they were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Challenge_League" title="Swiss Challenge League">Nationalliga B</a>. Zürich returned to the top league in 1990. The club did make it to last 16 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_1998%E2%80%9399" title="UEFA Cup 1998–99">UEFA Cup 1998–99</a>, but were beaten by <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">Roma</a>. The club won the Swiss Cup in 2000, beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Lausanne-Sport" title="FC Lausanne-Sport">Lausanne</a> in the final and also in 2005 beating <a href="/wiki/FC_Luzern" title="FC Luzern">Luzern</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_years">Recent years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Recent years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 May 2006, FCZ ended their 25 years wait for a league title with a dramatic final day victory against <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a> to win the Super League. They won thanks to a goal scored in the 93rd minute by <a href="/wiki/Iulian_Filipescu" title="Iulian Filipescu">Iulian Filipescu</a>. The goal gave FCZ a 2 – 1 victory and secured the title on <a href="/wiki/Goal_difference" title="Goal difference">goal difference</a> over <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Swiss_Super_League" title="2006–07 Swiss Super League">2006–07</a>, they also won the league.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Swiss_Super_League" title="2007–08 Swiss Super League">2007–08 season</a>, FCZ finished in third place. In the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Swiss_Super_League" title="2008–09 Swiss Super League">2008–09 season</a>, they won the league, edging out <a href="/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys" title="BSC Young Boys">BSC Young Boys</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Swiss_Super_League" title="2010–11 Swiss Super League">2010–11 season</a> FCZ finished second.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Swiss_Super_League" title="2015–16 Swiss Super League">2015–16 season</a> the club finished last, one point behind <a href="/wiki/FC_Lugano" title="FC Lugano">FC Lugano</a> and was relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Challenge_League" title="Swiss Challenge League">Swiss Challenge League</a>. Four days after the final game of the season FCZ won the Swiss Cup beating FC Lugano 1:0.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg/200px-Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg/300px-Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg/400px-Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Letzigrund_und_Umgebung.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Letzigrund" title="Letzigrund">Letzigrund</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Local club <a href="/wiki/Grasshopper_Club_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Grasshopper Club Zürich">Grasshopper</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a>, are the main rivals of FCZ. Due to the intense rivalry, these matches are so-called "High Risk Games," with an increased <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Switzerland" title="Law enforcement in Switzerland">police</a> presence in and around the stadium.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Z.C3.BCrich">Zürich</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Zürich">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since its inception, FCZ has always had a fiery relationship with neighbouring club Grasshopper over sporting supremacy in the city. Grasshoppers are known as the club of the elite and FCZ are known as the club of the workers. The matches between the two clubs are known as the only true local derby in Swiss professional football.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_vs._FC_Basel.2C_13_May_2006">Final vs. <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a>, 13 May 2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Final vs. FC Basel, 13 May 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before the last round of the 2005–06 Swiss Super League, Zürich were three points behind <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a> in the league table. The last game of the season was contested by these two clubs vying for the league title at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Jakob_Park" title="St. Jakob Park">St. Jakob Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>. <a href="/wiki/Alhassane_Keita" title="Alhassane Keita">Alhassane Keita</a> scored the first goal for Zürich. In the second half, <a href="/wiki/Mladen_Petri%C4%87" title="Mladen Petrić">Mladen Petrić</a> equalised. <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a> were seconds away from the title when in the 93rd minute, <a href="/wiki/Florian_Stahel" title="Florian Stahel">Florian Stahel</a> passed the ball to <a href="/wiki/Iulian_Filipescu" title="Iulian Filipescu">Iulian Filipescu</a>, who scored and made it 2 – 1 for Zürich. Zürich won the league title due to their superior goal difference. After the final whistle, the field was stormed by Basel supporters who also attacked Zürich players (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Basel_Hooligan_Incident" title="2006 Basel Hooligan Incident">2006 Basel Hooligan Incident</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FC_Z%C3%BCrich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
